<span id="freeTextContainer16432963250987558063">[4.5 stars]<br/>I got cheated, I thought that this is a nice boring story about a nice boy with a nice doggy who grows up to be a nice assassin in a nice castle. Well no one freaking mentioned all the angst and feels and the shit that goes down, and that spawn of Satan, Regal that needs to choke on a fish bone and die a most horrible death!!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509415642ra/24318041.gif' width='500' height='238' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Okay okay, let me take a breather and try to be coherent.. Obviously I loved this book to pieces (I mean I finished the almost 700 pages in 2 days), Robin Hobb ha</span>
  <span id="freeText16432963250987558063" style="display:none">[4.5 stars]<br>I got cheated, I thought that this is a nice boring story about a nice boy with a nice doggy who grows up to be a nice assassin in a nice castle. Well no one freaking mentioned all the angst and feels and the shit that goes down, and that spawn of Satan, Regal that needs to choke on a fish bone and die a most horrible death!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509415642ra/24318041.gif" width="500" height="238" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay okay, let me take a breather and try to be coherent.. Obviously I loved this book to pieces (I mean I finished the almost 700 pages in 2 days), Robin Hobb has a way of writing plot and characters that despite the slowness it just gets under your skin and you can never stop thinking about it. I love that in a series, if it gets me obsessed then I call it a success.<br><br>Plot is clearer in Royal Assassin, the villains become more fleshed out (AHH JUST THINKING ABOUT THAT ASSHOLE!), and the characters get even more depth.. Can we talk about how amazing Patience is? or how awesome it is that Robin Hobb wrote her back in the 90s to be a reincarnation of Helena Bonham Carter before she even became THE Helena Bonham Carter, which is probably one of the reasons I love Patience so much. All her scenes are either hilarious or just punches you in the chest.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509415642ra/24318042.gif" width="245" height="242" alt="Helena" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Burrich was another great surprise, I loved him in the second half of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1599367621?type=review#rating_137069699" rel="nofollow noopener">Assassin's Apprentice</a> but in this book, this dude is made of glory. Fitz of course is a no brainer, I'm reserving my overflowing gushing till he grows up a little bit because currently he is still in the emo hormonal teenage phase (think Order of the Phoenix) although quite understandable considering all the trauma he went through.<br>The Fool? one word: MORE! I need more of him, we only get a glimpse of his past in this book, and it's just enough of a tease to make us ask more questions about him! No one knows anything about his age, his sex, or what/who he is, and he only opens up (barely) to Fitz (<s>so I obviously ship it now</s>) and we do see more of him here, he's no longer always acting like a..well fool for lack of a better word, there's a quiet intensity to him, and oh my god I just love him and can't wait to peel more and more of his character's layers.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509417063i/24318116._SY540_.jpg" width="476" height="640" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>The fool by HerrMagermilch on <a href="https://herrmagermilch.deviantart.com/art/The-Fool-476473659" rel="nofollow noopener">Deviantart</a></i><br>Of course there's a bunch more of characters, Kettricken (BAMF and quite the inspirational speaker) and Verity (heart throb and glorious generally speaking).. <br><br><b>In conclusion, I'll reserve my heartiest recommendations till I finish the third book, but so far I've been pleasantly surprised by where the trilogy is going so far, I'm enjoying it thoroughly (along with the audiobook to help speed things up) and I honestly didn't mind the slowness and the repetition because the characters are what made this behemoth a huge win for me!</b></span>

<div id="review_900632125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900632125" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/900632125?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553573411" href="/book/show/77198.Royal_Assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer900632125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4425284990938246953"><b>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17295220-alexa' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alexa</a>!</b><br/><br/><i>Come, hunt with me, the invitation whispers in my heart. Leave the pain behind and let your life be your own again. There is a place where all time is now, and the choices are simple and always your own.<br/>Wolves have no kings.</i><br/><br/>After the harrowing experience in the Mountain Kingdom, FitzChivalry returns to Buckkeep and the Farseer court. Having barely survived his first real mission as a royal assassin, Fitz first vowed to renounce his oath to King Shrewd and abandon the shadow</span>
  <span id="freeText4425284990938246953" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17295220-alexa" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexa</a>!</b><br /><br /><i>Come, hunt with me, the invitation whispers in my heart. Leave the pain behind and let your life be your own again. There is a place where all time is now, and the choices are simple and always your own.<br />Wolves have no kings.</i><br /><br />After the harrowing experience in the Mountain Kingdom, FitzChivalry returns to Buckkeep and the Farseer court. Having barely survived his first real mission as a royal assassin, Fitz first vowed to renounce his oath to King Shrewd and abandon the shadowy world of intrigue completely, but his destiny eventually takes him back to the very place where his journey began, and back to the life of an assassin…<br /><br /><i>Royal Assassin</i> is more of what happened in <i>Assassin’s Apprentice</i>. We have the same enemy raiding the shores of the Six Duchies, inflicting the same horrors on the same people. We have the same antagonist, leashed but not put down. We have the same protagonist taking his lessons from the same people and essentially doing exactly what he did in the first book. And except for a character or two, there is little new.<br /><br />For the first seventy percent of this book (yes, <i>seventy</i>), nothing happened. The first book was also incredibly slow to get the plot moving, but really not this slow, and in that book it had a purpose: introduction of characters, plot and setting. In this one there is no excuse.<br /><br />The book also includes a lot of <i>horrible</i> characters. Fitz himself has become less likeable; Molly reminded me of a combination of Nynaeve and Egwene from Wheel of Time (to those of you who haven’t read my WoT reviews, that is about as bad as it can get); Chade has apparently become a stupid old man who is unable to see that his loyalty to his king must come before his loyalty to other members of the royal family; and the Fool has become blinded by his devotion to the same king.<br /><br />That does not mean that the book was completely horrible. Hobb’s writing is good, and at least some of the characters are interesting enough to read about. And while the first seventy percent were utterly and completely boring, the last thirty were the complete opposite, with intrigue and death and excitement around every corner. Another positive thing was Fitz developing his abilities with the Wit, and even finding a strong companion who was one of the most interesting characters of the book.<br /><br />Overall though, this was in my eyes a rather typical case of second book syndrome. The first book was great and I hope the third one will live up to it, but <i>Royal Assassin</i> was unfortunately just not good enough.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4425284990938246953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1032597471" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1032597471" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408028716p2/17295220.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa">Alexa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006480105" href="/book/show/68487.Royal_Assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17295220-alexa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032597471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15557573757189938147"><b>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26681101-markus' rel='nofollow noopener'>Markus!</a> Who unlike me, wrote a coherent and thoughtful review you can read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900632125' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.</b><br/>----------------<br/>752 pages. <br/><br/>This book was 752 pages long.<br/><br/><b>ARE YOU FREAKING KIDDING ME?!</b><br/><br/>Dune is less than 752 pages.<br/><br/>If you combine The Fellowship of the Rings and The Two Towers together, it's still less than 752 pages. <br/><br/>And in both cases, even with the comparable page count they managed to condense a LOT of story between their covers.<br/><br/>In this case we had 752 pages of filler. Very little happened, and the </span>
  <span id="freeText15557573757189938147" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26681101-markus" rel="nofollow noopener">Markus!</a> Who unlike me, wrote a coherent and thoughtful review you can read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900632125" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</b><br />----------------<br />752 pages. <br /><br />This book was 752 pages long.<br /><br /><b>ARE YOU FREAKING KIDDING ME?!</b><br /><br />Dune is less than 752 pages.<br /><br />If you combine The Fellowship of the Rings and The Two Towers together, it's still less than 752 pages. <br /><br />And in both cases, even with the comparable page count they managed to condense a LOT of story between their covers.<br /><br />In this case we had 752 pages of filler. Very little happened, and the plot almost didn't move. You could have condensed the action in what? 200 pages? Here's a resume of what happens: <br /><br />Fitz bonds with a new animal. <br />There's a "romance" angle that I hated.<br />Verity goes on a quest.<br />Regal is still the bad guy.<br />We still don't know anything about the red ships. <br /><br />That's mostly it. There are plot lines here and there that are left unresolved, and the book ends with a very interesting twist. But most of it was insufferably boring and I only finished it because I was buddy reading it with a friend. <br /><br />I will still read the next book, because I really liked the first one and I want to know what happens with the red ships. But I'm not sure I'll read anything else in the Elderlings series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15557573757189938147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66198914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7789170625248483305">Holy crap, that was a good book. I made the mistake of reading until past my bedtime to finish. Not only did I lose some sleep before starting a work week, but I then gave myself a series of messed up dreams as my poor little brain processed the end of this book.<br/><br/>Damn.<br/><br/>Not a lot I can say without spoilers. But Hobb is definitely moving up a few spots on my author list. <i>Assassin's Apprentice</i> was a very good book. Intriguing characters in a (seemingly)simple but interesting world with a good story. </span>
  <span id="freeText7789170625248483305" style="display:none">Holy crap, that was a good book. I made the mistake of reading until past my bedtime to finish. Not only did I lose some sleep before starting a work week, but I then gave myself a series of messed up dreams as my poor little brain processed the end of this book.<br /><br />Damn.<br /><br />Not a lot I can say without spoilers. But Hobb is definitely moving up a few spots on my author list. <i>Assassin's Apprentice</i> was a very good book. Intriguing characters in a (seemingly)simple but interesting world with a good story. It made me want to read more of the story of Fitz and the world of the Six Duchies.<br /><br />But this damn book made me HAVE to read more about Fitz and the Six Freaking Duchies. Where Book 1 was a little slow moving as Hobb set up the characters and the overall plot, this one does not hold back. It's not a roller-coaster ride, not until the last few chapters at least. But it's definitely one that keeps interest all the way through. <br /><br />Hobb's strength is her characters. Especially in how they relate to one another. She creates emotional bonds between them that are <i>real</i>. When these characters hurt, so does the reader. There's not just disappointment when something bad happens to a beloved character, but the pain of loss. <br /><br />Intrigue. Twists and turns. Betrayals. Unexpected WTF? moments. Even the occasional burst of humor. Everything I read a book for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7789170625248483305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007562268" href="/book/show/22016387-royal-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2803104140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5180161378056970721">Actual rating 4.5/5 stars. This is the second instalment in the Farseer Trilogy.<br/><br/>Fitz: royal bastard, royal assassin, royal pain. He returns to life at court only partially recovered from consuming poison, but the new perils awaiting him won't wait for his full health. His low status is an ever-present focal point but his emerging abilities and confidence leave his figure exposed to both new threats and new admiration.<br/><br/>Book one hurtled through the younger years of Fitz's life, but book two took it</span>
  <span id="freeText5180161378056970721" style="display:none">Actual rating 4.5/5 stars. This is the second instalment in the Farseer Trilogy.<br /><br />Fitz: royal bastard, royal assassin, royal pain. He returns to life at court only partially recovered from consuming poison, but the new perils awaiting him won't wait for his full health. His low status is an ever-present focal point but his emerging abilities and confidence leave his figure exposed to both new threats and new admiration.<br /><br />Book one hurtled through the younger years of Fitz's life, but book two took its measured time on a smaller portion of his education and upbringing. It built upon the political and magical foundations that were introduced in the former instalment and heightened the intrigue and complexity of both. This slower-pace of narrative was also an equal match for the deep exploration of character and relationships, which featured throughout. The first half of this felt especially stunted in action, but this only ensured more room for emotion and understanding to blossom.<br /><br />Fitz and the ever-elusive Fool already garnered my support in book one, but Nighteyes was added to the top of this list in book two. Romantic interest Molly was an interesting personality, already introduced in the first book but provided with more page space here. However, the oft-repeated romantic mooning towards her character was unfortunately not the addition I desired from this series.<br /><br />Asides from this small source of discontent, this was a thrilling second series instalment and the tumultuous ending has me eagerly grasping for book three before I have even properly digested all that occurred here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5180161378056970721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1488497939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007562268" href="/book/show/22016387-royal-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1488497939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2277005668924866345">I went into this second book of The Farseer Trilogy being a little bit sceptical. I'd heard a lot of people claiming that it contains too many pages and a lot of dull passages. I do see where those people are coming from, but even though not every page is action-filled, I still really really enjoyed it. <br/>In this book, I grew even more attached to Fitz as well as the heavy cast of characters that are introduced in this sequel. I felt like Robin Hobb juggled a lot of more balls in this story which </span>
  <span id="freeText2277005668924866345" style="display:none">I went into this second book of The Farseer Trilogy being a little bit sceptical. I'd heard a lot of people claiming that it contains too many pages and a lot of dull passages. I do see where those people are coming from, but even though not every page is action-filled, I still really really enjoyed it. <br />In this book, I grew even more attached to Fitz as well as the heavy cast of characters that are introduced in this sequel. I felt like Robin Hobb juggled a lot of more balls in this story which gave the world and the book more depth. I grew so attached to the characters that this is one of those books that I kind of regretted finishing. I wanted to continue reading about them - thank God there's a sequel to this one as well! <br />If you liked the first book in this series, I highly recommend this one as well. In my opinion, it was even better than the first one, and I'm eager to see where this is going after THAT ending! </span>
  <a data-text-id="2277005668924866345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2770851384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2770851384" />
    <a title="Anish Kohli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli"><img alt="Anish Kohli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579696384p2/20963257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2770851384?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anish Kohli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anish Kohli" href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli">Anish Kohli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6352142-royal-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20963257-anish-kohli?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2770851384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7649145132129846581"><b>
  <blockquote>“Are you sure you’ve not had a bad dream?”<br/>“If I have, it’s lasted most of my life.”</blockquote>
</b> Let me start the review by saying something very, very heartfelt: DAMN YOU, Hobb! Damn you! Not in a bad way bcz of course I love you. But damn you, woman!! Have you no heart? Dammit!! My poor Fitz!!<br/><br/>Gosh, this book is so so character centric that I dare say I have never read a book like this before and I barely know how to review it. It’s been well over a month since I finished the book and I just don’t know </span>
  <span id="freeText7649145132129846581" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“Are you sure you’ve not had a bad dream?”<br>“If I have, it’s lasted most of my life.”</blockquote>
</b> Let me start the review by saying something very, very heartfelt: DAMN YOU, Hobb! Damn you! Not in a bad way bcz of course I love you. But damn you, woman!! Have you no heart? Dammit!! My poor Fitz!!<br><br>Gosh, this book is so so character centric that I dare say I have never read a book like this before and I barely know how to review it. It’s been well over a month since I finished the book and I just don’t know how to review it bcz I wanna say so much but it’s all a mess in my head bcz gosh dang<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518748085ra/25068443.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am still aching for Fitz and everything that’s gone down in Buck Keep. I know this review will not be upto my own standards but well, I’ll still try bcz I wanna, really really wanna, gush about this book. Yes, it’s that good!! <b>
  <blockquote>“Here we are, and here is always the place we must start from.”</blockquote>
</b> <u>
  <b>Plot &amp; Pacing</b>
</u><br>This book, second in the series, picks up right where the first book left us off. With Fitz in the Mountain Kingdom and in grave danger. Meanwhile the Red Ships are wreaking havoc on the Six Duchies and not only are they helpless against the attacks, they are still no closer to knowing why they are being attacked or what the Red Ships want or how to make them stop.<br>Fitz has his own sets of problems, both inside the court and outside it. And this is the story of how he faces them and what he makes of himself in all the adverse situations and so much more. I wish I could talk plot more freely without being spoilery but I can’t. I might let slip something without meaning to so I will stop.<br><br>The pacing of this book is definitely very slow and as engaging as the book is, it is hard to ignore how slow it really is. When you’re done reading a book of 670+ pages, you expect a lot to happen but there are no major event happening in this book and yet, it’s constantly moving and building upon things and characters. There is so much politics and shady games and maneuvering that you keep reading. I definitely expected more in terms of what happens in the book but unfortunately I didn’t get it. The story barely moved forward in terms for marked events but at the same time the story was never stagnant. Does that make sense? Like if you ask were there any battles or if the enemies were vanquished or even identified or anything, the answer is no. But at the same time the story is not at a standstill and something is always happening. Does that make sense? Do even I make sense? Gosh! <br><br><u>
  <b>Writing</b>
</u><br>I mean who needs me to tell that the writing is great? And that Hobb is an amazing author? I guess everyone knows that already! But you know what? Damn these good authors! Damn Hobb! Why? Bcz these damned good authors set the bar higher and then the next book I pick isn’t upto the mark and then the people reading my reviews think I am a snob or something! Like my current read, A discovery of Witches, is perfectly fine but it’s not upto the Hobb mark and damn it do I want the Hobb mark! What am I gonna do now? <br>Anyway, like I said, writing part is pretty much great and I have no complaints on this front. Love how Hobb writes and I really want to read more books from her. Dare I say slowly I am becoming Hobb fan? I think I do. Yay, I guess?<br><br><u>
  <b>Characters</b>
</u><br>Gosh dang, what do I do in this section of the review? How many characters do I mention? Bcz there are so many! Alright let me try to keep it all short and make a mention of the important ones. And I’ll start at the top. <br><br><b>King Shrewd:</b> <i>
  <blockquote>“I know how you serve me, even when you are brimming with anger at me. I could ask little more than what you have given me.”</blockquote>
</i> Let’s just say that he truly was what his name said. He was a taxing king and a very strong character but this book contrasts him with just what he was and what he turned into. Even though he was barely a king or shrewd anymore, there were flashes of the man that we met in the first book and I liked this character. <br><br><b>Regal:</b> <br>I think the mark of any negative character is that you <i>hate</i> them. You hate them vehemently and you want to throttle them and want them to suffer. I found myself feeling that way for Regal and that goes to show how very well fleshed out the character of Regal was. Although as negative as he may be, he isn’t the antagonist of the series in the true sense. <br><br><b>Verity:</b><i>
  <blockquote>“Justice. There’s a thing we shall ever thirst after, and ever be parched. No. We content ourselves with law.”</blockquote>
</i> Verity is a great character. He might seem foolhardy on the surface, someone who is asking for trouble but when has that not been the case for anyone who wanted to do the right thing. Verity’s character isn’t the strongest on the surface but I think he is one of the strongest characters of the book to do what he does, day in day out, without any recognition or reward. He has an enviable resilience but then he also has an insufferable helplessness about him. A prince he may be, but he is far from a King as a person can be. Verity is a follower, not a leader. And his lack of desire to be a King shall be his undoing. <br><br><b>Burrich:</b><i>
  <blockquote>“The fight isn't over until you win it, Fitz. That's all you have to remember. No matter what the other man says.”</blockquote>
</i> Now this is one character I really like. Burrich is the person Fitz derives strength from, even if he doesn’t know it himself. Burrich is every bit a father to Fitz as he could be given the circumstance. Burrich has a strength about him and I find him a badass in his own way. <br><br><b>Fool:</b><i>
  <blockquote>“No man is so dangerous as the man who cannot decide what he fears.”</blockquote>
</i> One of <i>THE MOST</i> engaging character I have ever read. And unpredictable! Fool is tons and tons of fun and he is always on about something meaningful and logical even if a person doesn’t get it. What the fool suffers through in this book, I feel really sad for him and it wasn’t pleasant to read. It’s great to read just how much of a devoted servant he is/was to the King Shrewd. <br><br><b>Kettricken:</b><i>
  <blockquote>“It is an odd language, yours. You speak of passing time as in the Mountains we speak of passing wind. As if it were a thing to be gotten rid of.”</blockquote>
</i> Now here is a queen-in-waiting if I ever saw one. But then that’s all she is. Not a queen yet and neither fit to be one. Kettricken is a strong woman in her own right and I like her character. She truly is a good match for Verity and she will be instrumental for him if he is ever to rule. I understood Kettricken’s motivations and her reasons and I liked how she carried herself but at the same time I kind of found her too rigid for not undertaking a few changes that could help her better. I think she could have helped herself and her husband quite a bit by just doing some things that she might not really like. But then I guess that that’s true strength. Staying the way you are when it is hardest to do so. <br><br><b>Nighteyes:</b><i>
  <blockquote>“Wolves have no kings.”</blockquote>
</i> Love, love, love Nighteyes and his bond with Fitz! I absolutely adore his passions and his portrayal and I just love the fact even more that Nighteyes is a wolf (yes, I have an unhealthy obsession with wolves) and I really enjoy how casually he treats Fitz at times and even defies him. He feels like a brother, like he says. Not a servant. I want to see how this goes forward. <br><br><b>FitzChivalry:</b><i>
  <blockquote>“Fitz? What will you do?”<br>Tears stung my eyes. I blinked, and it passed. “What I am told,” I said heavily. “When have I ever done otherwise?”</blockquote>
</i> You know, I realized this in the very first book itself that Hobb is not one of those authors who give their protagonists an easy time. Infact, if anything, she is the exact opposite of that but in this book she is downright torturous! She’s put poor Fitz in completely impossible situations where nothing he does will ever be right or will ever make anything better or easier. She puts him through hell and then some. In two books she’s brought him close to certain death twice. And although you always know he’s gonna be fine bcz Fitz is the one writing down these stories as an older person, it’s not pleasant to see him faced with death. Hobb makes him suffer thoroughly! From physical abuses and beatings to emotional and mental trauma, Fitz suffers it all. And he still keeps going. There are instances where I almost feel like he might snap but he doesn’t. He is embroiled in court politics and intrigues and saving the Six Duchies and saving the King and saving the Prince. From saving people to murdering people, he does it all. This burden is far too heavy for his shoulders but man, does he try his best. But then it is also this part of his character that doesn’t allow me to form a real and lasting bond with Fitz. I don’t see his reasons for staying. He could leave. Go away. Far away. Start a life and just put all this mess behind him. But for some reason he keeps pushing and I don’t see that reason very clearly. I think this is one point where I find Hobb is lacking. But I loved the last bit with Fitz towards the close of the book where he goes after Serene! I found that really good. Very dark in its own right but a great sequence for sure. <br>However, I am very interested to see what Hobb will do to/with Fitz now that she has ended the book on the note that she has!<br><br><u>
  <b>Magic System</b>
</u><br>For the first time in any of my reviews I am adding this section separately. I am doing so bcz I hope to read more complex systems as I go forward from here but mostly bcz of the fact that after this book I am actually feeling confused about the magic system here. <br>I am confused as to what the hell is happening with the Skill. Fitz can’t Skill on purpose but he can actively guard himself against it? Isn’t’ that just using the Skill? Also I don’t understand that how was Justin a threat to his mental barriers when even Verity couldn’t get through? <br>As far as the Wit is concerned, I find it a bit confusing how Nighteyes almost forced bonded to Fitz. Can animals do that?<br>And there is absolutely nothing concrete on the Elderling front either, is there?<br>Basically the magic system is pretty open ended, I feel. There aren’t many rules laid down and not much focus is given to it either. I would like Hobb to build more on this bit too bcz I find the system intriguing enough all though it’s limited in the sense of what can be accomplished through the Skill. I suppose this won’t change in the books going forward, will it?<br><br><u>
  <b> Overall impact</b>
</u><br>This is a great book with much heartbreaking moments for the characters you are concerned with. It also manages a couple of small twists and turns and I think this book is a great addition to the trilogy and it has set up the stage very amazingly for the concluding part and I hope it is a fabulous one! The world building isn’t the most detailed one but it’s pretty great and the setting as well. I think this is a worthy sequel. And I loved reading this book even if at times I felt it was a bit slow and dragging. <br>I think, what really makes this book really special for me, doubly so, is the fact that I have finally found an author who writes in the first person POV and still makes me love their writing style and also the fact that at long last, I have a fav lady author who I really love reading from and that too fantasy! It’s great and I think I shall read much more from Hobb and I hope she will end the trilogy in a masterful manner so that I can’t resist picking up the next series from her. You go Hobb! <b>
  <blockquote>“They had no right to do this to me. I had not been born to be their tool. I had a right to live my life freely, to be who I was born to be. Did they think they could bend me to their will, use me however they would, and I would never retaliate? No. A time would come. My time would come.”</blockquote>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7649145132129846581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3426906362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3426906362" />
    <a title="Claudia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20498957-claudia"><img alt="Claudia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507465969p2/20498957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3426906362?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudia" href="/user/show/20498957-claudia">Claudia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780593157923" href="/book/show/49499207-royal-assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498957-claudia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498957-claudia?shelf=z-to-a-hobb">z-to-a-hobb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498957-claudia?shelf=art-photography">art-photography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3426906362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer867177615833047864">I really took my time with this one, reading just a chapter or two in the evening, but eventually it came to an end. <br/><br/>I enjoyed it to the max despite all the horrors Fitz had to put up with. His relationship with Nighteyes is the best part. The one with the Fool is still slowly developing, Kettricken turns out to be one of the most beloved characters and Regal the most hated.<br/><br/>The third one can’t come soon enough, because I am resisting now the urge to start the third in any other edition; I want t</span>
  <span id="freeText867177615833047864" style="display:none">I really took my time with this one, reading just a chapter or two in the evening, but eventually it came to an end. <br><br>I enjoyed it to the max despite all the horrors Fitz had to put up with. His relationship with Nighteyes is the best part. The one with the Fool is still slowly developing, Kettricken turns out to be one of the most beloved characters and Regal the most hated.<br><br>The third one can’t come soon enough, because I am resisting now the urge to start the third in any other edition; I want this illustrated one, to enchant my eyes with the beautiful images and fonts and colours. <br><br>Here are some from this edition:<br><br>Nighteyes 💖<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595609699i/29859277._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fitz &amp; Molly:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595609699i/29859278._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Kettricken:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1595609699i/29859279._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fitz and Burrich:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[

<div id="review_1146596036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1146596036" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1146596036?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006480105" href="/book/show/68487.Royal_Assassin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1146596036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4276180956681743453">Robin Hobb's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/41452-farseer-trilogy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Farseer Trilogy</a> and rest of the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/54099-realms-of-the-elderlings' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Realm of the Elderlings</a> series are very highly rated on Goodreads scoring 4+ average rating for each individual volume. Very few fantasy series can boast this kind of average rating. Ms. Hobb also does a great job of promoting her books by interacting with her readers through social media websites like Reddit. I find her to be friendly and approachable and always happy to recommend books by other authors. <br/><br/>Royal Assassin is the second book of the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/41452-farseer-trilogy' rel='nofollow noopener'>F</a></span>
  <span id="freeText4276180956681743453" style="display:none">Robin Hobb's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41452-farseer-trilogy" rel="nofollow noopener">Farseer Trilogy</a> and rest of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/54099-realms-of-the-elderlings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Realm of the Elderlings</a> series are very highly rated on Goodreads scoring 4+ average rating for each individual volume. Very few fantasy series can boast this kind of average rating. Ms. Hobb also does a great job of promoting her books by interacting with her readers through social media websites like Reddit. I find her to be friendly and approachable and always happy to recommend books by other authors. <br><br>Royal Assassin is the second book of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41452-farseer-trilogy" rel="nofollow noopener">Farseer Trilogy</a> and follows directly without a pause for breath from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45107.Assassin_s_Apprentice__Farseer_Trilogy___1_" title="Assassin's Apprentice (Farseer Trilogy, #1) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Assassin's Apprentice</a>. In this book, our hero FitzChivalry finds himself increasingly beleaguered by the evil prince Regal and his henchmen. The entire book is set in Buckkeep the capital of the “Six Duchies” kingdom. Fitz finds love, a new animal soul mate, new allies and further develops his facilities for “Skilling” and “Wit” (magical / psychic abilities). None of these help him to avoid having the stuffing beaten out of him, but at least he manages to get in a couple of good jabs. With this kind of plot-heavy adventure tale the less I reveal of the plot the better I believe.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470120111i/19888960._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Fitz as depicted in the 2009 edition of <i>Royal Assassin</i><br><br>The storyline of this series is refreshingly original in that it does not follow the standard epic quest story arc even though it does follow the development of the protagonist from childhood to adulthood. However, it is not strictly speaking a bildungsroman as it is also a story of court intrigues and a seemingly unwinnable war with mysterious invaders who can convert (“Forge”) normal people into emotionless subhumans. The fantastical elements in this series (so far) is quite subtle, there is no wizard blasting people with wild magic, turning people into newts etc. The magic in this book is more akin to the “psi powers” we see in sci-fi books or superhero comics, telepathy, shared minds, psychic battles and whatnot. There is also the mysterious magic of “Forging”. <br><br>Characterization as with the first book is very well done, all the characters are believable. Fitz has a very hard time of it with the odds always stacked against him. As with a lot of fantasy books, the colorful supporting characters tend to be more interesting than the protagonist. With this series, the most fascinating character is The Fool who is wonderfully enigmatic and eccentric with an idiosyncratic way of speaking. I imagine his dialogue must be quite difficult to write. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470120299i/19888971._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>The 2016 edition of <i>Royal Assassin</i>*<br><br>Ms. Hobb’s writing is very clean and a pleasure to read. It is difficult to explain the virtues of this kind of writing, the prose style is not highly literary or lyrical, yet it is graceful and lucid. There is not a word out of place and the whole thing reads very smoothly, no jarring or clunky dialogue to stumble over. This writing style reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16094.Lois_McMaster_Bujold" title="Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Lois McMaster Bujold</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14032.Connie_Willis" title="Connie Willis" rel="nofollow noopener">Connie Willis</a> whose prose is always a pleasure to read. While the book is quite grim and violent in places I would not rank her among the likes of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R_R__Martin" title="George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">George R.R. Martin</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/276660.Joe_Abercrombie" title="Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">Joe Abercrombie</a> as a purveyor of “grimdark”, super edgy fantasy novels, the violence is less graphic and there are no sex scenes to speak of. Her plotting, pacing and world building is very skillful and meticulous. She is also very clever with her cliffhanger and I am now very much looking forward to the concluding volume of this trilogy. After that I will no doubt go on to the second, third etc. trilogies of this lengthy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/54099-realms-of-the-elderlings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Realm of the Elderlings</a> series. That should keep off the street for a while.<br>__________________<br>* With wraparound cover art by John Howe. Sorry, no idea who John Howe is, obviously a very talented artist. These <a href="http://subterraneanpress.com/store/product_detail/the_farseer_trilogy" rel="nofollow noopener">new Far Seer Trilogy editions</a> are also specially priced (but not in a good way!).</span>
  <a data-text-id="4276180956681743453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gMeN9+ARfqqUxNLnc8mCY1itS92TRUhCk5tX9KFyMP6tmslCQVDdnLPgQSmvTj70OHr9A/+/EVH21okzeaiaFQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4546610528117946672">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 st</span>
  <span id="freeText4546610528117946672" style="display:none">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 star from me means,yes, I liked the book, and I'd loan it to a friend and it went everywhere in my jacket pocket or purse until I finished it. A 3 star means that I've ignored friends to finish it and my sink is full of dirty dishes. A 4 star means I'm probably in trouble with my editor for missing a deadline because I was reading this book. But I want you to know . . . I don't finish books I don't like. There's too many good ones out there waiting to be found.<br /><br /><br />Robin Hobb is the author of three well-received fantasy trilogies: The Farseer Trilogy (Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest), The Liveship Traders Trilogy (Ship of Magic, Mad Ship and Ship of Destiny) and the Tawny Man Trilogy (Fool’s Errand, Golden Fool, and Fool’s Fate) Her current work in progress is entitled Shaman’s Crossing. Robin Hobb lives and works in Tacoma, Washington, and has been a professional writer for over 30 years.<br /><br />In addition to writing, her interests include gardening, mushrooming, and beachcombing. She and her husband Fred have three grown children and one teenager, and three grand-children.<br /><br />She also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/53255.Megan_Lindholm" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Lindholm</a>, and works under that name have been finalists for the Hugo award, the Nebula Award, and the Endeavor award. She has twice won an Isaac Asimov’s Science Fiction Readers’ Award.</span>
